## Reply 135 — participant_026 · 2024-08-13 · post-29826155

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> le cur said: Now this is really cool. How does the income transfer work? Does it depend on the Holding having a given ruler, potentially a camp follower you choose to leave behind as steward? Does it stop (or potentially stop) if the Holding is seized during war? Is it inherited by subsequent generations of Adventurer? And finally, is it possible to found other types of Holding, perhaps a Temple or a City? Given you don't necessarily own the holding itself, it doesn't feel that implausible to establish another type, particularly if certain conditions are met. For instance, it could be possible to establish a Temple holding but only if your Devotion is sufficiently high and you share the same Faith as the host County, whereas you can establish a City provided you have either City Keepers or perhaps one of the Parochialism/Republican Legacy Traditions. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Wokeg said: With Found a Holding, you’ll be able to leave your mark on the places you visit, and gain passive income for your trouble, or even steal a county out from under the local ruler. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
Mulling over the raid issue and I do get why people are so incensed about the decision. But I also see why you didn't want to just outright enable raiding. I think there are possible short-term and long-term solutions here. The short-term solution, which would be way more feasible to implement in time for the release, would be to add another possible condition for giving up your titles. If you're a Freebooter with Gallowsbait, settling down as a ruler would grant you a special Upstart Freebooter trait which lets you return to adventuring even if you don't have any Tenet or Tradition enabling it. That'd let you do raiding to a degree: you can't raid as an Adventurer, but you can seize a small piece of land and use that as a base for your raiding activities. The longer-term, i.e. much harder to implement but potentially more satisfying and interesting, solution is that certain Baronies can be designated as Pirate/Bandit Havens, and Adventurers can raise raiders provided their Camp is located in a Haven. Then, instead of simply stealing wealth right away, or even when you cross into the border of your host realm, you have to bring it back to the Haven you've chosen as a base. This would also give landed rulers the benefit of knowing where potential raids will come from, allowing them to plan ahead. A few of these Havens could exist at each start date - for instance, Rugen in 867, Socotra in both starts - but more could be created dynamically, for instance through the Kingdom of Mann and the Isles decision. Under certain circumstances, independent rulers (or perhaps vassals under Level 1 Crown Authority) can cede a non-capital Barony to Freebooters (or perhaps simply let them build a Holding, since that's already an option), whereafter the Barony has a permanent Haven modifier and operates somewhere between a Republic vassal and a Holy Order lease. A Haven could have certain benefits, like increased income (perhaps even a cut of the raiders' loot) or development, but also a malus to Control growth, increased Plague risk and diplomatic penalties with whoever gets raided. Sure, they don't raid you, but they do invite counterattacks from your neighbours, and that's not great for stability. As such, you'd be tempted to get rid of them... which would, of course, significantly upset any raiders who have used the Haven in the area. In the worst case scenario, if a Haven's rulers are well-prepared, they'll try to seize the whole County for themselves, forming some kind of pirate state - see, for instance, Gotland in the 14th century - which might just operate as a Tribal realm, but could also run on its own special Government form. That would also provide an interesting alternative for Freebooter characters looking to gain landed status: accept that you won't have the prestige of a Feudal ruler, and instead join your local Haven in the hopes of becoming their leader. It would also encourage Freebooter characters to found their own Holdings, since they can then use them as a base for further raiding. On that note, my last reply is also relevant here: I'm not sure how I'd want the Havens to work - whether it's exclusively a type of leased Barony, or whether it's just a special modifier applied to any Holding. The former is cleaner, but the latter adds more opportunities for pirate rulers like the Kingdom of Mann and the Isles, who can automatically gain a Haven in their capital without the pros and cons of a leased Haven vassal. However, especially if it is the former case, then I definitely think the Holding type should factor into it. Specifically, as a Freebooter looking to establish your own Haven, you should only be able to establish a City. Perhaps, if you're establishing the Holding in a Tribal realm, it should instead be another Tribe holding, and in that case it wouldn't require City Planning. Oh yeah, come to think of it: You say "leave your mark" here. Does that mean I'll be able to pick a name and possibly a coat of arms for the Holding even if I don't rule the County? Or is that not viable? At the very least, it'd be nice if there was some indicator of who founded it - perhaps the default coat of arms could be quartered with the arms of my adventurer company.

## Reply 137 — participant_096 · 2024-08-13 · post-29826188

Since there basically was a secret bonus dev diary in the reserved top-post last week, I just wanted to gather my thoughts on what was discussed there that otherwise wouldn't be followed up on. I'm still quite surprised this is a DLC gated feature. Really feels like a "Retinues in CK2" level mistake, considering we tend not to see DLC features touched up or iterated on (cough Royal Court cough) and this is such a map wide feature. A lot of the dev comments gave me the tone of, "Yeah, would have been a cool idea... No time though " and it is like, well now there is really no time since this is DLC content that will never be improved. This really feels like it was intended to be the "Update Half" of the DLC (not calling it a "lesser half" obviously, considering the clear amount of work put into it, but as the half more important to the long term gameplay experience, like the Culture update) and perhaps some shenanigans occured behind the scenes. Responses to Specific Responses: Why did you decide to make mercenaries mostly not use these features at all, because they might move around, instead of just making 2 or 3 mercenaries in a region specifically not move? I think that it could be a cool idea to have a Seneschal court position task, like you can toggle between having them handle contracts (as if an AI char) or letting you take direct control of it, as a way to get the landed players interact with the contract system if they want (which basically half the responses were apologizing for lacking). If there is a simple debug command to make any courtier an adventurer, why not just include that as a button at the custom character screen or just after game start? Yes please on Supply Map Mode (perhaps bundled with Raid/Loot map mode). The lack of cohesion between the Viking Adventurers and R2P adventurers continue to exacerbate my concerns about CK3 becoming the "horse designed by committee camel". All these independent systems clunking along with no interrelation (except back to vanilla) makes for a very strange experience. I strongly think CK needs to learn from Stellaris's amazing Custodian initiative in this regard (and perhaps take the more radical step toward eventually "vannilifying" older and underperforming DLC so new DLC can utilize their worthwhile mechanics) or the game will just start being an impossible recommendation to new players when I can't justify they try out the vanilla game when there are so many very visible DLC holes. I think the idea someone suggested about being able to design camp followers is good (and could serve double time to let us design our spouse and children too). Additionally, the idea of perhaps having hireable other realms like tribal governments on the "Special Mercenaries" tab is intriguing for future content I had the high honor of being the final question asked in the Q&A, and I greatly appreciate the communication the developers of this game have with the community, especially for the development cycle. In response to the answer to my question, where I asked for some clarification on what is Update vs. DLC content, I do feel like, while really good that these systems are open DLCless to modders, it does seem like, from my understanding, it will be rather difficult for them to do anything with them without basically rebuilding everything from the ground up? Without any of the contracts actually being in vanilla, TC mods will have to bizarrely dance around things like mercenaries, or make their own bespoke version of them that also plays chicken with touching the DLC files, in a way that I think will just stifle these systems being used at all. Look, I've bought the season pass, I've already paid for these features (which is slightly why I feel less embarrassed about writing such a long message), so I'm not begging for free stuff when I suggest you reconsider what stuff goes into the Update and what goes into the DLC this time when it comes to landless. Even just making only mercenary adventurers and some limited relevant contracts vanilla I think would be enough, and the most justifiable since they are the adventurers that kind of sort of already exist, unlike say the scholars or wandering mystics. Elsewise, I fear this DLC's legacy will become more about it what it never became and what it stifled, rather than what it is. And now, I have to respond to this diary...

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Wokeg said: Losing Your Last Title​Lastly you can, of course, always become an adventurer the classic way that I’m sure you were all expecting: if you lose your last county (and you’re not an Administrative family), you’ll be given the option to continue with that character by forming an adventuring band instead of game overing or switching to someone new. The AI will sometimes do this too, if their personality suits it. This can be a result of title revocation, conquest, or even exile. If a character’s last title is stripped away, and they’re either a player or a suitably driven individual, then you may see them pop back up as an adventurer. > le cur said: One last thing: this Dev Diary has solidified my conviction that Northerner Armies ought to be modelled as Landless Adventurers, even if they're not fully integrated into the system. That is to say, I think that even if you want to continue spawning in the 10k-strong death stack, they should at least belong to a proper Landless Adventurer which is attacking you via the Adventurer Duchy Invasion CB. Otherwise, I think my reply to the last Dev Diary more or less explains why I dislike having them as a unique phenomenon within the game. I do still think you could stand to integrate them fully into the Landless Adventurer system, for instance by letting Norse characters (perhaps with the right Adventure legacy, or otherwise with the Varangian Adventure CB) choose a special Varangian Adventure Camp Purpose which, somewhat like the Legitimists system, allows them to rapidly accumulate a large army while they're in Norse land at the cost of it all falling apart unless they launch an invasion within a short deadline. However, I also recognise why you chose not to do this, and your reply below is very illuminating. Even accepting this, I maintain that you ought to run them as Landless Adventurers, for the reasons I've described above. Yes, they're separate phenomena, but it makes much more sense to represent someone like Rollo of Normandy as an Adventurer from a gameplay perspective. The leaders of these Norse bands might not have been exactly like your average Landless Adventurer, but neither were Legitimists; you've still put them under that umbrella because you recognise that a Legitimist ruler is essentially an unlanded exile who happens to have a decent claim, and thanks to that claim they can accrue significant support. Similarly, the leader of a Northern warband is riding a wave of historical circumstances, but in their own position they are far more like a Landless Adventurer than a hardcoded mercenary army, and if it's possible to buy off a marauding Adventurer with free land and vassalage it should be possible to do the same to a guy like Rollo. On that note, it could be cool to give rulers an option or two to sweeten the deal against sufficiently frightening invaders: Feudal rulers could offer a more generous contract, for instance, and all rulers could offer a Hook to slightly increase acceptance. Like offering vassalage, except you're bargaining at sword-point so you can only ever decrease observations. Perhaps you could even offer other incentives, like a hostage exchange or a betrothal, but I appreciate that might be a hassle to include in a single UI. Click to expand...

<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
This is definitely an on-going concern; we've not done anything here this DLC AFAIK but we're gonna need to address it at some point. Honestly I'd just like to add increased levy toughness/damage with increasing cultural eras so that they scale over time, but discussions about warfare tend to get bogged down because the balance there is... contentious. Happy to help! I'm afraid that hybrid cultures require you to hold at least one county also, so no (ditto divergence). Glad to hear it! Probably not, if I'm honest. Never say never, but a mechanic like this is likely to see a lot of traffic from players, so any time we got for expanding it I'd imagine we'd put into extending variability for adventurers. You can definitely play as you heir, assuming you've got someone. Or indeed someone else, you get various options now. In order: Afraid not — some day, who knows, we might be able to put them into regencies, but certainly not abdication. Adventurers have a fair bit more content with duels to the death as (largely optional) side ventures, via events and contracts, so we force it to come up a bit more than usual. Y'know, I'm not sure what the AI weights are atm (this was very much a team effort and that interaction was a different designer) but what we're aiming for is that it should happen some of the time but not be constant. We're playtesting this stuff in more detail ahead of release atm. Largely being on opposing sides in wars; another adventuring band doesn't have too much to offer you vs. landed rulers. Bit varied: they can take non-gold payment (which may sometimes be markedly cheaper), sometimes they're just good chaff available for not that much money because they're getting started, sometimes they've grown much larger than other merc bands and can really turn the tide. Essentially, an ordinary mercenary band is reliable but basic, an adventurer is unreliable for availability but has a much broader range for what they've got on offer. Nothing specific but I'd be a little surprised if we didn't; we only originally intended them for adventurers and mid-way through development the Byzanteam went "oh, these are neat [yoink]", so I can easily see that happening again. Yes. Honestly, the thing I fought hardest for that came out the best IMHO was camp purposes. The MVP version of adventurers were just mercenaries, which I felt would be leaving out a huge section of the fantasy for many people, so that was probably what was net most fun for me. Actually a sucker for how Hereward turned out, personally. He's not printed it yet, I believe. Soon. I hear you and I completely understand your disappointment. If we could've made it work without completely borking the economy, we would have. It is perfectly fair to say the feature doesn't hold appeal for you without a thing you were reasonably looking forward to, and I hope that admin still offers you what you'd like. Liiiiiitle bit too unlikely, I'm afraid. Glad you liked it! This one took just a smidge longer than the other one, as the source matter was a bit more eclectic and I had to double check a lot more stuff handled by other folks, so the kind words are appreciated. Yes, you can be a target, though atm mercenaries generally won't switch sides on you. Tbh I'd like to do more with that, but I'm doubtful we'll get the time (unless someone gets to it in PDT at some point). We experimented with it a bit, but same as employers stiffing their mercs, it was difficult to get the balance of fun vs. frustration to a good point. Honestly, extremely valid points all round here. We've got an eternal tension between people who've been playing CK for twelve years (... Jesus H. Christ kill meeeee why is linear time so cruel), sometimes longer for the CK1 veterans, the people who've been playing CK3 long enough to have basically mastered it, the people who play it once every couple of years and have fun, and the newbs flowing in over time. The title needs to appeal to & cater to all of them, but (IMHO) too often we end up softening up challenges or harsh realities because they can be frustrating for the latter groups. It starves the long-term players of attention, and to my mind, that's our spiritual core — certainly the group I place myself into. I'm a little optimistic that some of the changes we're making to inheritance and playing within a dynasty means we'll be able to offer a bit more challenge to all players in future, but I'd definitely agree that this lack of serious setback is a knotty problem we should try harder to deal with. Though I mean, saying that, last time I tried to personally we got harm events and those got such a nuclear hate reaction from so many people that I wound up virtually disabling them by default. Some of that was pretty fair — we really should let you tag into a different character when you get incapable — but a lot of it was just outrage at the idea of death taking you randomly, which I was not expecting. You can start this way but we can't really narratively or mechanically support you doing it forever. :/ I'm afraid that, as you can't be your own knight, so see an army of 1 dude you'll need at least one subordinate to go to war on your behalf. Sure, I can put a slight provisions cost reduction on 'em. Don't think we did that but eh. Though I think I did give exemptions for Saharan cultures to the Sahara's new provisions hellscape modifiers. Spread, no, travel through/flee like crazy from, yes. Despite the occasional plague body-toss in the odd siege, biological warfare in that way not really a thing in our period. Heh, mebs another time. Damn it, I've not seen the anime. ... legitimists we did initially plan to make available for all, but when we started on them it rapidly came together that it'd be a lot more tonally consistent to gate them to higher tier claims. Afraid not; this is both to help with repetition and to reflect that the role you set yourself is very much self-imposed. Scholars won't generally act as mercs but, well, if they've got enough troops because they have them as travel guards (I did actually set some adventurer-specific travel danger events to not fire if you have sufficient, albeit higher than you'd realistically need, troops: not every fool attacking a large travelling army), then the coin does spend just as well. Nae worries; two adventurers marrying follows the usual messy logic for married rulers. Their camps stay separate (though I... suppose there's potential room for some kind of merge-camp interaction, admittedly not for release), and children start at the camp of whoever is the dominant marriage partner, or else the character birthing them. I... don't know how that work in an mpreg scenario off the bat, which I believe we support for mods at least but I could be misremembering. We actually did look into this — it's already possible for rakes after all — largely because I thought we could mebs come at medieval sex work from a really interesting POV compared to the usual landed snobbery. Unfortunately, it was a scoping casualty, so adventurers are restricted to rakes-only just like everyone else. There is a single camp upgrade for having a semi-private area for your courtiers, for those who prefer not to be intimate with an audience. Afraid not this time. I'd love to see playable knights eventually and we've got some modding support that should connect a few more bits of the warfare system together + some more MaA-centric effects'n'triggers (should enable a lot of wonderful jank for folks in mods in the meanwhilst) but it hasn't undone the code block on players being knights. I've done some very cursed stuff with some of the new support. I... don't think we've mentioned it anywhere but sod it, wasn't getting it's own DD anyway: we've got a deterministic conquest setting for England in 1066 that ends the war in whoever you select's favour the first time battle is joined, which involved wrangling some code support from a kindly wandering programmer. Again, not something that took development resources — I was getting just the littlest bit worn down by the adventurer grind and wanted to make something for me, so took a few evenings to add this, as I've wanted it since pre-release. Not at present, I'm afraid. I'll make a note and see if it's potentially something we can look into for a patch. Succession, no, player character, yes. This is what the Choose a New Destiny feature does. That doesn't really solve the UX problems or the issue of positioning your camp somewhere OP in advance. I appreciate the helpful input, but trust me, this was not solveable with the resources we had. Definitely not hybrid with Ancient Egyptian, they're millennia away from that (at best I guess you could say Cleopatra but I think that's a very liberal reading of just having a pharaoh on the throne as being "ancient"), but yeahhhh, Egyptian is in an awkward spot. I don't think anyone's happy with the current set-up (not miserable, but I'm sure we can all agree that it's... lacking resolution, y'know?) but we've yet to sit down and hash out a better solution that we're happy with. It's really, really welcome to be able to have these types of discussions with folks from time to time (even though I fear I'm gonna be less able to get into the weeds with you about this just now, I just wanted to call out that... yeah this is a wonderfully presented take IMHO). That said, as discussed a bit last DD, I don't think we can or should represent Scandinavian Adventurers using this system. It'd be complicated implementation involving multiple DLCs overlaying each other just for the sake of unified presentation, which doesn't feel like a good use of time, and that's not even getting into the implied need to represent landless military powers using the same system in future: what I might actually be able to sort (at some point!) is an active offer settlement option for such rulers. I did add an event for this in the FP1 post-release patches (I forget which one), but it's fairly dependent on continually raiding/trading with the same place, so it's highly player-dependent tbh. In retrospect, an interaction would've been a much better way to service that, and provide you the fantasy of ruling over Rollo rather than necessarily just imitating him. I can look into it, at least. I would genuinely love to see more lateral outcomes to wars like this. I'm a firm believer in the victory-white peace-defeat mechanic as a way of keeping players honest and giving the AI a shot by hard-setting wargoals (vs, say, sniping their capital to cripple their economy like that literally every happened in our period), but that absolutely shouldn't preclude rulers coming to agreements like this. We don't play enough with ways to finish off wars outside of the core dynamic, and in particular buying off hostile powers in believable ways and various forms is just so, so, so tonally appropriate and mechanically satisfying for everyone involved. <3 Extremely glad it appeals, and I hope it at least somewhat matches the hype. And finally a request since we can also get scholarly adventurers, here is a request for a really interesting one from 11th century who was also a member of one of the powerful dynasties at the time Mahmud al-Kashgari who was a member of the ruling dynasty of Karakhanids, believed to be the grandson Bogra Yagan Tegin, who had to flee due to court intrigue. His grandfather wanted to abdicate in favor of Mahmud's father but one of his wives poisoned several members of the family to put her own son Ibrahinm on the throne and several other members, including Mahmud al-Kashgari fled after this. He believed that the new khans men were after him for a long while so he constantly moved around. We've got an eternal tension between people who've been playing CK for twelve years (... Jesus H. Christ kill meeeee why is linear time so cruel), sometimes longer for the CK1 veterans, the people who've been playing CK3 long enough to have basically mastered it, the people who play it once every couple of years and have fun, and the newbs flowing in over time. The title needs to appeal to & cater to all of them, but (IMHO) too often we end up softening up challenges or harsh realities because they can be frustrating for the latter groups. It starves the long-term players of attention, and to my mind, that's our spiritual core — certainly the group I place myself into. I'm a little optimistic that some of the changes we're making to inheritance and playing within a dynasty means we'll be able to offer a bit more challenge to all players in future, but I'd definitely agree that this lack of serious setback is a knotty problem we should try harder to deal with. ## Reply 162 — participant_026 · 2024-08-13 · post-29826314

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Empocariam said: I'm still quite surprised this is a DLC gated feature. Really feels like a "Retinues in CK2" level mistake, considering we tend not to see DLC features touched up or iterated on (cough Royal Court cough) and this is such a map wide feature. A lot of the dev comments gave me the tone of, "Yeah, would have been a cool idea... No time though " and it is like, well now there is really no time since this is DLC content that will never be improved. This really feels like it was intended to be the "Update Half" of the DLC (not calling it a "lesser half" obviously, considering the clear amount of work put into it, but as the half more important to the long term gameplay experience, like the Culture update) and perhaps some shenanigans occured behind the scenes. <snip> In response to the answer to my question, where I asked for some clarification on what is Update vs. DLC content, I do feel like, while really good that these systems are open DLCless to modders, it does seem like, from my understanding, it will be rather difficult for them to do anything with them without basically rebuilding everything from the ground up? Without any of the contracts actually being in vanilla, TC mods will have to bizarrely dance around things like mercenaries, or make their own bespoke version of them that also plays chicken with touching the DLC files, in a way that I think will just stifle these systems being used at all. Look, I've bought the season pass, I've already paid for these features (which is slightly why I feel less embarrassed about writing such a long message), so I'm not begging for free stuff when I suggest you reconsider what stuff goes into the Update and what goes into the DLC this time when it comes to landless. Even just making only mercenary adventurers and some limited relevant contracts vanilla I think would be enough, and the most justifiable since they are the adventurers that kind of sort of already exist, unlike say the scholars or wandering mystics. Elsewise, I fear this DLC's legacy will become more about it what it never became and what it stifled, rather than what it is. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Empocariam said: Why did you decide to make mercenaries mostly not use these features at all, because they might move around, instead of just making 2 or 3 mercenaries in a region specifically not move? Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Empocariam said: The lack of cohesion between the Viking Adventurers and R2P adventurers continue to exacerbate my concerns about CK3 becoming the "horse designed by committee camel". All these independent systems clunking along with no interrelation (except back to vanilla) makes for a very strange experience. I strongly think CK needs to learn from Stellaris's amazing Custodian initiative in this regard (and perhaps take the more radical step toward eventually "vannilifying" older and underperforming DLC so new DLC can utilize their worthwhile mechanics) or the game will just start being an impossible recommendation to new players when I can't justify they try out the vanilla game when there are so many very visible DLC holes. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Wokeg said: I'm a firm believer in the victory-white peace-defeat mechanic as a way of keeping players honest and giving the AI a shot by hard-setting wargoals Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
I kind of agree with you here; they run the risk of becoming progressively more dated over time, or alternatively of making the base game progressively less playable. That said, it's worth noting that EU4 has previously made DLC features public as they become necessary to play subsequent updates, so it's possible Paradox will do the same. I think my ideal compromise would be having Landless Adventurers technically playable, but with basically no options available, perhaps even just stuck to playing as Wanderers or Mercenaries with only a single contract type. Apart from anything else, it means you'll be able to expand on the possible Landless Adventurer options in later DLCs without requiring that people also own Roads to Power - for instance, a future Asian content pack might piggyback and expand on the existing system to enable wandering ascetics. Have to say I think they're right to make most mercenary companies fixed. Admittedly it's a bit weird to have parallel mercenary systems, but apart from anything else the Adventurer mercenaries will rise and fall in power quite significantly, and I suspect that if they all ran on the Landless Adventurer system you'd have serious problems with players getting outcompeted for contracts. I'm glad others agree on this, though I do also see what Wokeg's getting at with the most recent reply. On that note: Come to think of it, that could be an option. At the moment White Peace is fairly meaningless for the Northerner Army - it's basically identical to a defeat for the Norse, but for some reason the defender doesn't get to tout nearly as grand of a victory. Perhaps the White Peace could let you vassalise the Northerners in exchange for a significant hit to Legitimacy. Having said all this I'll continue to advocate moving the Northerner Army onto the Landless Adventurer system, especially because I've now talked myself into believing there should be Landless Adventurer content that doesn't require this DLC to run. In an ideal world, I'd hope that a Norse player with Northern Lords could go Landless and subsequently raise the mighty Northerner Army for their own use, but I appreciate you will have greater priorities for the foreseeable future. Enjoy your Dark Heresy!

## Reply 163 — participant_096 · 2024-08-13 · post-29826315

As far as I know, our policy remains that we'll post dev diaries when we have a DLC coming up or something else interesting to say (like the yearly reviews). Fillers/teasers/non-development stuff has just caused headaches, so they're likely to be sparsely posted if at all. I wish they didn't, but they do, and the light grumbling of infrequent-yet-meaty DDs easily beats the flame wars and conspiratorialising that have resulted from segmented or filler DDs. At the end of the day, if writing certain DDs isn't helping development and only seems to aggravate parts of the fanbase, then the simplest solution is to just not write those DDs. Apologies that I can't give you a more optimistic answer. Edit: speedy reminder that I don't control the DD schedule/policy here, so please take my opinions with a grain of salt. Aww, thank you. Honestly, I think these days we try to focus a bit more on stuff that's more visible to the player: attention to detail is great but if it comes at significant cost for a reward most won't notice, it's just not giving people good value. Not to say that we don't try to be accurate or work with historical detail, but it's gotta be tempered by how much time you spend on it. ... which I say politely ignoring the vizier extravagance modifier script from late last year. Made in collaboration with a very diligent researcher and we uhhh, got slightly carried away with it. Ooph, landless? That would be a lot of technical work for even the basics, honestly. The tragic thing is, I think you're utterly correct. This wasn't an issue pre-release/immediately after release. We knackered our early communication strategy hard and now we've gotten ourselves stuck in a toxic loop that sucks for everyone, where the best solution so far has been to just abstain for long periods of time. It is what it is, I guess. Maybe we'll break it some day, but I don't see that happening any time soon. Very much this, though with the qualifier that things've been getting a lot better on that front for the last year or so for a whole host of factors. This is true, it did come after a prolonged period of little communication from us — the last big thing we'd said (IIRC) was that we wouldn't be saying much until we had something important to say. There's an argument to be made that maybe we should've stuck more rigorously to that, not launched a teaser two weeks before an announcement, but then... we get a lot of requests to post more teasers, more WIP stuff, more just discussion of what we're working on, so we figured we'd chance it somewhere safe after we'd fairly recently telegraphed that a DD would mean more DDs and something imminently announcing. It didn't go well, c'est la vie, but if a teaser bombs because it didn't come ahead of a larger announcement then the key learning there is that that type of teaser isn't really worth while, let alone something that has nothing on the heels for months yet. Honestly, folks these days seem like they're having a lot more fun with the cryptic hints that Community puts out than anything dreamt up by Design. Which, tbh, makes sense: we're awkward nerds who generally don't do great at public speaking, they're awkward nerds who do. Case in point: we have people in this thread who've said they'd prefer to have filler DDs, we've had people who've said they'd not mind WIP DDs, and (if I may assume a little here) here we've got someone saying that really all they want is something talking about solid mechanical improvements. All valid views, all valid wants, and I'm by no means suggesting that any of y'all posting atm are being anything less than lovely. Just, we extrapolate this out to a larger community, you add a few bad apples that spoil the discussion or hyberbolise thinks out of context for Reddit, and you see how we end up in a scenario where the only winning move is not to play. ## Reply 169 — participant_116 · 2024-08-13 · post-29826363

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Unlike landed rulers (even tribals), adventurers don’t pay to maintain their troops. It’s assumed that they’re paid partially in provisions, partially in loot they take as you move, and partially in a share of the gold paid by your contract givers. As with not expending provisions when not travelling, this was something we went with after our early testing: gold can be very feast-or-famine for adventurers, so if they have a steady expense but are having trouble finding even irregular income (or, as is usually the case, simply aren’t getting paid in advance), they rapidly become extremely frustrating to play. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
Sooooooooo, I kind of hate this. Loot, even when you're traveling scholars? A share of the contract that doesn't change whether you have 100 men or 10000? In general, these are the kinds of decisions that make CK3 sometimes fall flat for me. Something was frustrating so you handwaved it. Comes across less as finding a solution and more like deciding we can just pretend a problem doesn't exist. At the very least there should be some way to model the discontentment of sitting around with a large army and not doing anything with it. If you're not even pursuing contracts, you should get something like the Warmonger "too long at peace" penalty and see followers become discontent or soldiers deserting. Maybe a large group can forage in a specific spot for a long time, but it's going to wreck the place and make the local rulers mad at you. I would rather there be some gameplay here rather than, we're just not going to model that tbh.

I really think you should consider other options such as the one I presented rather than just making it so we can’t raid at all and can only be Mercs. The title needs to appeal to & cater to all of them, but (IMHO) too often we end up softening up challenges or harsh realities because they can be frustrating for the latter groups. ## Reply 211 — participant_147 · 2024-08-14 · post-29826956

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Wokeg said: Honestly I'd just like to add increased levy toughness/damage with increasing cultural eras so that they scale over time, but discussions about warfare tend to get bogged down because the balance there is... contentious. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
It would be nice if there was a variety of effects (originating from Government type, Laws, Traditions, Tenets, Innovations, Geography, etc) that could buff or debuff Levies in each particular Realm, so rulers in different situations could be more or less incentivized to rely on Levies in relation to Men-at-Arms and Mercenaries, and there were important strategic tradeoffs to army composition. Historically, we see that societies that had a large population of freeholding farmers who could afford weapons and armor and were culturally/politically incentivized to serve as soldiers (such as the Roman Republic) could field huge conscript armies, whereas societies that lacked this had to rely on different methods of raising an army and securing its loyalty.

## Reply 222 — participant_158 · 2024-08-14 · post-29827122

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Simple enough, as it happens. You can expel any adventurer from your realm (including your domain and any of your vassals’ lands) via a character interaction, which will stop contracts from generating there, force them to leave, and force them out if they ever end up back there. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Once an eviction has been accepted (or white peaced in the war), any lands controlled by the evicting ruler can no longer be travelled to by the adventurer. They can be travelled through, largely for mechanical reasons, but cannot be used as an end destination and won’t generate contracts till the opinion expires (say, through a convenient assassination). If an adventurer ends up in lands they have been exiled from for any reason, they are automatically re-routed out of them again. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
... it isn't reasonable for the king of France or Holy Romen emperor to be able to ban you from the whole kingdom / empire, they didn't have that level of control. Realistically rulers should only be able to ban people from their directly held counties and maybe duchies, and have to rely on their vassals to enforce the ban on their lands. If your lover, the duke of Aquitaine, is willing to shelter you the king of France shouldn't magically be able to bar or evict you from Aquitaine. (Of course if the Duke of Brittany is loyal to the king of France he should uphold the ban) (yes I posted this on Reddit, I realized after doing so that it was more likely to be read here)

## Reply 225 — participant_161 · 2024-08-14 · post-29827158

I saw a comment on Reddit which I thought would be brilliant, I'm wondering if it's something you guys could look into: Legitimists are one of the things I've wanted most in this game. It should be way easier for deposed rulers to challenge usurpers. English history is full of exiled princes building their strength across the channel before returning to try and take the throne (my boy Edward IV even did it twice). This has always technically been in the game through claimant courtiers, but I've pretty much never seen the AI actually act on a courtier's kingdom casus belli. Having a dedicated mechanic should hopefully give the AI the nudge necessary for them to actually pull the trigger. The one thing missing would be the ability to have legitimist and/or opportunistic vassals in the claimed kingdom lend support to your cause. It'd add a lot of interesting political gameplay if you could negotiate an agreement with potential Warwicks and Clarences to overthrow a low-legitimacy monarch.

I think this system needs reworking, at least for landless characters. Maybe it could be tied to troops or level of prestige. Can Greek Administrators abandon their estate and become Landless Adventurers? Perhaps if their estate is damaged enough by a siege there could be an event where you could choose to stay and rebuild or abandon your estate and adventure? Can you marry your followers off to wandering commoners and other adventurers’ followers? Or peasant courtiers of rulers? Is it possible for your followers to mutiny against you? Is the Fishing event a part of the hunting activity? IMO, it would make sense for it to just be a new form of hunting, like how Falconry was added in T&T. Finally, I do find it weird that the landless adventurers is part of the DLC instead of the free update. It seems like a great baseline that could easily be expanded upon in later updates/DLC. Gating it behind the DLC makes it less likely to be expanded upon in the future. Like wandering merchants could use this system in the future. Or for pirates/privateers if CK3 ever gets a naval update. Or for Holy Orders when Theocracies get an update. When a Steppe DLC comes out, there could be decisions that let you transition from Landless Adventurer to Steppe Nomad by uniting adventurer camps or gaining enough followers. I understand making the Byzantine content and administrative government DLC-locked, but locking the Adventurer system behind this seems like a missed opportunity that will be an issue within a few DLC.

In small realms this makes sense but when you get to the scale of the HRE it is silly. This is only reasonable if we are talking about mercenary companies: it is much harder for a few hundred soldiers to be discreet than a dozen scholars.

I don't believe we've done any contracts that require two DLCs at the moment: I've said it a bit elsewhere, but by the time we had what we felt was a contract system that was fun to play with, our priority became making sure there was as much variety within it as possible. Contracts locked to other DLCs would've run fairly contrary to that, even though most CK players buy most DLCs AFAIK. They're mechanically possible and mebs something that could be considered in future, but weren't relevant for us this time. Inheritance actually always overrules that, which does apply here. ## Reply 297 — participant_007 · 2024-08-19 · post-29835925

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> riadach said: Sure while you're here, Toirdelbach Ua Briain, prospective (/actual) king of Munster. Will he make it in as landless? (bit of info here, to flesh him out: https://forum.paradoxplaza.com/foru...ke-toirdelbach-a-landless-adventurer.1699597/) Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
He has not — sadly we're pretty committed to Murchad occupying that spot these days. He's got a billion tutorials as the starting dude + the actual in-game tutorial that'd need updating + got the Legends of CK update. :eyes: As I personally felt we shouldn't constrain an obvious historical correction largely for approachability (and uhhh, I guess hoping that I don't trigger that one dude who wants us to stop adding these) I did add a game rule for toggling between, if you'll pardon the indulgence, "historical" & "classic" modes. Classic is the default vanilla, you keep Murchad. Historic puts Toirdelbach in his rightful place, fudges the stats around to be a bit more reflective of the historic situation, and, if you selected playing as Murchad, tags you into Toirdelbach instead. Murchad is then dumped in a swamp. Best I could do. Figured it's not a big deal for everyone but it'd matter to me, so it's there for other folks who'd like it corrected in vanilla without having to download a mod just to fiddle around with that.

## Reply 302 — participant_007 · 2024-08-19 · post-29836027

<!-- artifact:quote:start -->
> Duarte said: Toirdelbach get's the special treatment but Michel III doesn't? Paradox confirmed Iconodules. in a more serious note can micheal III of byzantium get the same choice it's a long sticking issue, and plenty of people would appreciate the choice. Click to expand...
<!-- artifact:quote:end -->
I'm afraid Michael III also gets a special event: we start off with Basileios murdering him. Picks up close to the end of the comic and mirrors some of the loc from it, with a lil gloss explaining that he's dying a bit earlier than he did historically for gameplay reasons. Basileios then gets to decide what he wants to do with the man's memory (which, here, sets his nickname so that you don't have to set history against him as "the Drunkard" forever more), so you can at least decide whether you want to take a leak on his grave after tossing him into it. Alas, we only have the morphs for cutting off one hand, so Michael keeps his right in the event. Hoping to get a follow-up event in for the situation with the children buuuuut didn't quite manage it for release. So, yes, icons rule, iconoclasts drool. Edit: actually, I realise that "for gameplay reasons" is a rubbish explanation — basically Toirdelbach and Murchad are easy to swap because there's no historical expectations and the de facto structure of Munster is extremely simple in 1066. The same thing with the last Amorian is a bit tricksier because it's a much larger empire and an advanced murder plot that only wins out sometimes is gonna give us wildly variant of Byzantium in 867 a lot of the time, plus it makes Michael incredibly sucky to play because you basically have to meta. I actually don't think that that's insurmountable, we could probably script around it without too much fuss if we tried, but the Makedonians are a lot more popular than the Amorians so the general community sentiment has always been in Basileios' favour vs. Michael's, whereas everyone looking at Murchad vs. Toirdelbach either isn't particularly fussed orrrrr wants Toirdelbach because he's the correct character. The former is a conscious choice, the latter is just a mistake, basically.

If I could, instead, swap to his heir in mid reign, and go on landless adventures while my now-AI-controlled father/former character makes bad AI decisions and screws up the realm I stand to inherit, that would be so awesome. It would provide a significant boost in both fun and challenge during the mid and late-game run doldrums, I think.

## Reply 327 — participant_208 · 2024-08-26 · post-29847158

I just had a thought about how a landless character might become a raider. I get that the whole "adventurer loots province they're in" thing doesn't work. But most pirates historically had a base of operations, even if they didn't control it. So it could work something like this. An adventurer treats the province they're in as "friendly" territory for purposes of being able to switch their army to raiding. That also grants that province and all others in that realm as immune to raiding. Both the top level ruler and the county title holder receive opinion penalties for the targets of raids launched by adventurers in their territory. Raiding would also generate gallowbait. There would be pressure on the ruler of the host county to expel the raiding adventurers, but adventurers could counter that by ensuring that the ruler likes them (possibly by sharing some of their loot) and also by targeting people the ruler hates. This wouldn't allow for a maurading band of adventurers to just strip the land as they move about, but it would allow players to play as pirates, finding rulers who are amenable to hosting raiding adventurers and have nearby enemies with lots of loot. This all might be too much to include at this date, but at the very least I could see raiding contracts where rulers hire adventurers as privateers to raid their enemies (and take a share of the loot, naturally).
